  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f9507924-6e9e-46af-85e5-dd787565408a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText4902500137465712310" style="display:none">Ruby Oliver is 15 and has a shrink. She knows it’s unusual, but give her a break—she’s had a rough 10 days. In the past 10 days she:<i><br /> lost her boyfriend (#13 on the list), <br /><br /> lost her best friend (Kim), <br /><br /> lost all her other friends (Nora, Cricket), <br /><br /> did something suspicious with a boy (#10), <br /><br /> did something advanced with a boy (#15), <br /><br /> had an argument with a boy (#14), <br /><br /> drank her first beer (someone handed it to her), <br /><br /> got caught by her mom (ag!), <br /><br /> had a panic attack (scary),<br /><br /> lost a lacrosse game (she’s the goalie), <br /><br /> failed a math test (she’ll make it up), <br /><br /> hurt Meghan’s feelings (even though they aren’t really friends), <br /><br /> became a social outcast (no one to sit with at lunch)<br /><br /> and had graffiti written about her in the girls’ bathroom (who knows what was in the boys’!?!). </i><br />But don’t worry—Ruby lives to tell the tale. <span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">these are the ones i found in the boyfriend list!!<br/>- Taxi Driver<br/>- Movies where the couples hate each other half the time: Ten Things I Hate About You. <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">these are the ones i found in the boyfriend list!!<br />- Taxi Driver<br />- Movies where the couples hate each other half the time: Ten Things I Hate About You. One Fine Day. When Harry Met Sally. You've Got Mail. Intolerable Cruelty. The African Queen. Addicted to Love. Bringing Up Baby. The Goodbye Girl. How to Lose a Guy in 10 Days. As Good As It Gets. French Kiss. Groundhog Day. A Life Less Ordinary.<br />- Movies where after breaking up, it turns out the man actually loves the women madly and can't exist without her: Pretty Woman. An Officer and a Gentleman. Bridget Jone's Diary. The Truth About Cats and Dogs. Reality Bites. Jerry Maguire. Persuasion. High Fidelity. Say Anything. Notting Hill. Grease. Four Weddings and a Funeral. Runaway Bride. <br />- Nightmare on Elm Street<br />- Carrie<br />- Movies where the apparently hopeless dorky guy who's been there all along eventually gets the girl: The Wedding Singer. Dumb and Dumber. When Harry Met Sally. There's Something About Mary. Beauty and the Beast. While You Were Sleeping. Revenge of the Nerds. Lots of Woody Allen movies. (ew) <br />- The Breakfast Club<br />- Everything You Always Wanted to Know About Sex But Were Afraid to Ask<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_54459486" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54459486" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54459486?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385732062" href="/book/show/1259132.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54459486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4628344563638202295">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/04/the-boyfriend-list-by-e-lockhart.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>I can't help it, I simply adore <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart' title='E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>E. Lockhart</a>'s YA books. As far as girly, chick-lit books about relationships go, hers are the best. And this is coming from a person who isn't into chick-lit.<br/><br/>Just like in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6937999.Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks__The' title='Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks, The by E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart' title='E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>E. Lockhart</a> explores the challenges of being a teenage girl. In “The Boyfriend List” we learn about Ruby Oliver through her relationships with boys (not necessarily her boyfriends), how these relationship affect her life</span>
  <span id="freeText4628344563638202295" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/04/the-boyfriend-list-by-e-lockhart.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />I can't help it, I simply adore <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart" title="E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">E. Lockhart</a>'s YA books. As far as girly, chick-lit books about relationships go, hers are the best. And this is coming from a person who isn't into chick-lit.<br /><br />Just like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6937999.Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks__The" title="Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks, The by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart" title="E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">E. Lockhart</a> explores the challenges of being a teenage girl. In “The Boyfriend List” we learn about Ruby Oliver through her relationships with boys (not necessarily her boyfriends), how these relationship affect her life and if they are at all healthy and constructive. <br /><br />Ruby is not a perfect character – she makes mistakes, she hangs on to boys for all the wrong reasons, she doesn’t appreciate her real friends enough. In short, she does everything that other teenage girls do. But in the end, through looking back at her dating history, analyzing her own family dynamics and talking to her therapist, Ruby learns how to be more assertive, get what she wants from her relationships with boys and simply becomes a more self-aware person.<br /><br />I can not praise Lockhart’s writing style enough – it is funny and clever. I like how the author deciphers relationships through Ruby's experiences. I love that the underlying message of this book is for girls not to become complacent and emotionally dependent on boys, that dating a popular guy is not the most important thing in the world. It is a sad thing to say, but I feel like many grown women need to read this novel, just to get a better understanding of their dating patterns and mistakes. Many still have no idea how to get what they want out of their relationships with men. This book is better than any relationship self-help book out there. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4628344563638202295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_303810638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/303810638" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/303810638?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385732062" href="/book/show/1259132.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who like books with REAL teenage characters</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nataliya by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter">for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303810638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2825187090052802287"><br/>Few things are worse than being 15 <i>(examples: nuclear war and dental work without anesthesia)</i>. <br/>As Stephen King said, <b>
  <i>"If you liked being a teenager, there’s something wrong with you."</i>
</b> But Ruby puts on her Big Girl panties and <b>DEALS WITH IT.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727503.jpg' width='200' height='140' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727504.jpg' width='200' height='140' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><i>No catatonia or glorified semi-suicidality. Instead, she sees a therapist, like a responsible young adult.</i> <blockquote>
<u>Why is being a fifteen-year-old girl so traumatic, you ask?</u> Some things that instantly come to mind: crippling insecurity and faltering self-esteem</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2825187090052802287" style="display:none"><br>Few things are worse than being 15 <i>(examples: nuclear war and dental work without anesthesia)</i>. <br>As Stephen King said, <b>
  <i>"If you liked being a teenager, there’s something wrong with you."</i>
</b> But Ruby puts on her Big Girl panties and <b>DEALS WITH IT.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727503.jpg" width="200" height="140" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727504.jpg" width="200" height="140" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>No catatonia or glorified semi-suicidality. Instead, she sees a therapist, like a responsible young adult.</i> <blockquote>
<u>Why is being a fifteen-year-old girl so traumatic, you ask?</u> Some things that instantly come to mind: crippling insecurity and faltering self-esteem, arbitrary but vitally important social rules, the need to fit in and be validated, bottled-up feelings always on the verge of exploding, carelessness bordering on cruelty, and finally, those alluring, mysterious, and incredibly frustrating boys.</blockquote> <b>Ruby Oliver is fifteen and, as the title suggests, is going through a tough time</b> (those statements are practically synonyms). Within a few days she goes from a reasonably popular and happy girl to a social pariah whose boyfriend has dumped her for her best friend, whose friends have turned away from her (and she alienated those who did not), and the whole school thinks she is a "slut". And she is getting all the blame (not the boy. Never the boy). <b>So now she has panic attacks and a poncho-wearing shrink.</b> And she just wants things to go back to normal.<blockquote>"<i>I just wanted the panic attacks to stop. And the hollow, sore feeling in my chest to go away. And to feel like I could make it through lunch period without choking back tears.</i>"</blockquote> I expected a light-hearted fun teen high-school drama with plenty of boy crushes, silly shallowness, teen girl gossip, and all sorts of hilarious misunderstandings. And, of course, some ceramic frogs.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727505.jpg" width="160" height="130" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727506.jpg" width="70" height="80" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727507.jpg" width="160" height="130" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the author of (also fifteen-year-old) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1629601.The_Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie Landau-Banks</a> delivers quite a bit more. <b>Her book has an unexpected depth that is not in any way suggested by a ridiculously-adorable-ceramic-frog book cover.</b> She writes a story that also encompasses the dangers of emotional lying to yourself, masking your feelings, and emotional passivity. It's a story of friendship and betrayal and unfairness. But it's not a love story. It's not a coming-of-age story about finding yourself, either. It's a story about heartbreak because of losing things you love. <b>
  <i>It is about learning to <u>DEAL WITH</u> plenty of nasty things life sends your way and keep yourself together, especially during the 'frogless' days.</i>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727508.jpg" width="180" height="140" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373768i/727509.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ruby's story is far from the way too common <i>"reader-please-insert-yourself-here"</i> wish-fulfillment fantasy.</b> For one, Ruby has plenty of faults that are real and not cutesy or charmingly imaginary (she can quite often be clueless, shallow, self-absorbed, and mean). <br><blockquote>"<i>My problem is I can think whatever I think—girl power, solidarity, Gloria Steinem rah rah rah — but I still feel the way I feel.<br>Which is jealous. And pissy about little things.</i>"</blockquote> <b>There is no fairy-tale ending:</b><br>- no cute previously misunderstood boy swoops in to rescue her from her troubles and make everything better;<br>- she does not do anything special to make everyone adore her;<br>- she does not discover the true meaning of life or have a life-changing epiphany;<br>- she does not become a markedly better and very-grown-up-for-her-age person;<br>- her friends don't magically understand her point of view and welcome her back with open arms.<br><br><b>What Ruby does learn is that some honesty and self-assertiveness goes a long way.</b> She sees how many people around her keep their true feelings bottled up - including her friend Nora and her own seemingly outspoken mother. Ruby is able to analyze her dating patterns and learn from them a bit. She learns that at least for a time being it is possible to step outside the boundaries of the shallow self-contained rich private school world. <b>She learns that sometimes fair is just not going to happen and you just need to move on.</b> She learns that even though your friends can be unfair and cruel, you still miss them and love them. <b>She misses the things she lost, and knows that the new things she came to appreciate cannot replace the losses. </b>She learns that the happy ending is not always in the works for you, and that's okay.<blockquote>
  <b>In short, she gets some (not very fun) lessons in adulthood. Things do not get magically great for her in the end, but they do get better.</b>
</blockquote> This book is written for teens, but it's not juvenile. It does not gloss over the 'uncomfortable' subjects - we get frank and positive expressions of teenage sexuality (including a footnote about oral sex and some quite long boob-squeeze), we get a couple of f-bombs and a scene of underage drinking without serious consequences. <br><br>The writing is very good. Overlying all the serious messages is the clear, snarky, and hilarious voice of Ruby, quirky and generously endowed with a sense of humor. There are smart references, a healthy dose of self-deprecation, funny anecdotes in the footnotes, adorable love notes from Jackson, and caring, well-meaning but absolutely clueless parents arguing whether Ruby has an eating disorder during her panic attack. <br>-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br><b>It's a refreshingly honest and funny book with a believable and relatable imperfect protagonist, with the writing that keeps you engaged in the story until the end</b>. A light read with surprising depth. <b> 4 stars.</b> And I already got my hands on the next story in the series!<br><blockquote>"<i>I was hoping there’d be a set of guidelines handed out in Sex Ed class, but Sex Ed—when I finally got to take it — was all about biology and birth control and nothing about anything that actually goes on between people. Like how to tell what it means when someone forgets to call you when he said he would, or what to do when someone gropes your boob in a movie theater.</i>"</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2825187090052802287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_169820652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169820652" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169820652?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169820652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14786722178438387863">I remember being 12 years old and thinking I was pretty much awesomeness personified for reading books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre' title='Jane Eyre by Charlotte Brontë' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jane Eyre</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights' title='Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wuthering Heights</a> when all the other kids were reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl' title='Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roald Dahl</a>. Since then I seem to be going backwards and reading all the books I should have read prior to my 16th birthday, like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_' title='Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> and also this one. And I love them! It just goes to show how a book doesn't have to be a couple of centuries old and a household name to be awesome.<br/><br/>I love</span>
  <span id="freeText14786722178438387863" style="display:none">I remember being 12 years old and thinking I was pretty much awesomeness personified for reading books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre" title="Jane Eyre by Charlotte Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Jane Eyre</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights" title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Wuthering Heights</a> when all the other kids were reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a>. Since then I seem to be going backwards and reading all the books I should have read prior to my 16th birthday, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_" title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> and also this one. And I love them! It just goes to show how a book doesn't have to be a couple of centuries old and a household name to be awesome.<br /><br />I loved Ruby Oliver and, as a former clueless adolescent myself, I also understood her. She doesn't colour over the truth, in fact her voice is refreshingly honest and so so funny. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart" title="E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">E. Lockhart</a>, for me, seems very good at portraying the newfound sexuality of a young girl, like with the realisation that, not only does Ruby not slap him and yell "ewww!" when Cabbie feels her up in the cinema, she actually likes it (shock, horror!). I think this is a great novel for teenage girls (and boys too, if they so wish), it addresses the 'slut' issue with humour and without being all up-in-your-face feminazi. It made me laugh and held underlying messages - it was always going to be a winner!<br /><br />It's probably a 5 star read if I'm honest but I always like to wait until I've read more when it's only the first in a series. Either way, thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2250020-tatiana" rel="nofollow noopener">Tatiana</a> for the reviews that made me read this great book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14786722178438387863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_303086267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/303086267" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/303086267?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Cassette 9781400098880" href="/book/show/1134041.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fluffy-books">fluffy-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303086267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1723344865680577034">I like this book so much for being a fun, frothy, escape about gossip and boys. But I LOVE this book for transcending <i>all</i> of those things. When I first read the title: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301022.The_Boyfriend_List_15_Guys__11_Shrink_Appointments__4_Ceramic_Frogs_and_Me__Ruby_Oliver__Ruby_Oliver___1_' title='The Boyfriend List 15 Guys, 11 Shrink Appointments, 4 Ceramic Frogs and Me, Ruby Oliver (Ruby Oliver, #1) by E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Boyfriend List: 15 Guys, 11 Shrink Appointments, 4 Ceramic Frogs and Me, Ruby Oliver</a>, I expected that this book would contain a few swoon-worthy boys and that our heroine Ruby would experience some drama-fueled teenage angst trying to decide which one to date. I even jokingly proclaimed myself “Team Noel” within minutes of the</span>
  <span id="freeText1723344865680577034" style="display:none">I like this book so much for being a fun, frothy, escape about gossip and boys. But I LOVE this book for transcending <i>all</i> of those things. When I first read the title: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301022.The_Boyfriend_List_15_Guys__11_Shrink_Appointments__4_Ceramic_Frogs_and_Me__Ruby_Oliver__Ruby_Oliver___1_" title="The Boyfriend List 15 Guys, 11 Shrink Appointments, 4 Ceramic Frogs and Me, Ruby Oliver (Ruby Oliver, #1) by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Boyfriend List: 15 Guys, 11 Shrink Appointments, 4 Ceramic Frogs and Me, Ruby Oliver</a>, I expected that this book would contain a few swoon-worthy boys and that our heroine Ruby would experience some drama-fueled teenage angst trying to decide which one to date. I even jokingly proclaimed myself “Team Noel” within minutes of the starting the book – fully expecting that I would spend the next day or so regressing into teenage girl-hood and gossiping about these characters. Now I feel like a shallow jerk for expecting so little from E. Lockhart, the brilliant woman who brought us Frankie Landau-Banks!<br /><br />So often, girls are encouraged to “be nice” and get along – to not make waves, to make do with whatever life throws our way, to never give voice to our negative feelings. <br /><br /><i>”My problem is I can think whatever I think – girl power, solidarity, Gloria Steinem rah rah rah – but I still feel the way I feel. Which is jealous. And pissy about little things.”</i><br /><br />Even mild discontent is often viewed as “bitchy” or “whiny.” These expectations are so pervasive and ingrained that we often place them on ourselves. I know I’ve been guilty of it – of quashing my anger, jealousy, and hurt beneath a pleasant mask, even as it all multiplies and festers inside. Because that’s what happens when you don’t acknowledge a negative feeling, in my experience: it grows exponentially until it comes out one way or another.<br /><br />In Ruby’s case, she starts manifesting those feelings in a very physical way: panic attacks. Her parents, who are both clueless <i>and</i> over-involved, sign her up immediately for therapy. The novel itself is a written account of Ruby’s thoughts about a list that her therapist asks her to create: of all the boys that she’s ever been involved with. But the boys aren’t the real story - it turns out that Ruby’s best friends have stopped speaking to her and she’s become a “leper” at school. The story unfolds organically from one flashback to another with the list and the scenes in the present providing a really nice anchoring framework. It feels fluid but logical at the same time.<br /><br />I am just so impressed at how much depth this fluffy little story had to offer. Ruby’s struggle to acknowledge and justify her own feelings and to eventually give voice to them is a subtle one. But as someone who has fought that battle, I really felt the weight of it. I’ve been there – so afraid of my own feelings that I couldn’t even acknowledge that they existed. When I was in that place, it felt like voicing those things – giving them a name – would only make them more horrible, more real.<br /><br />This isn’t a triumphant feel-good story, but a quiet one about one girl’s first small steps toward emotional honesty, with other people but mostly with herself. And E. Lockhart gives us so much more than just Ruby: there’s Kim, who holds her feelings inside until they erupt in vicious outbursts; there’s Ruby’s parents, who are engaged in a constant power struggle that they never discuss openly; and there’s even Nora at the end, who seems to want to forget that anything happened.<br /><br />I’ve already downloaded the next three books and I simply cannot wait to continue. I know from experience that once you’ve given voice to your feelings – once you’ve felt that relief and that realization that the world is in fact <i>not</i> going to end – it’s almost impossible to go back to holding them in. I can’t wait to see more of Ruby’s journey in these books.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Cyndi Lauper - <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sQtU5mWBlAI" rel="nofollow noopener">When You Were Mine</a><br /><br /><br />Woohoo! I get to match <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/caties-challenges.html" rel="nofollow noopener">one of my songs</a> so soon! This is one of my absolute favorites (I've got it on right now and my girls are having a dance party). It was written by Prince and Cyndi Lauper covered it but kept the male/female designations the same. This is my song for Ruby and Kim - because I know that Kim was awful and malicious, but I kind of hope they make it up by the end of the series - after a few cathartic talks, of course.<br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/03/ya-review-the-boyfriend-list-by-e-lockhart.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1723344865680577034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_311884497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311884497" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311884497?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Regina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=listened-to-audio-only">listened-to-audio-only</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=only-listeneed-to">only-listeneed-to</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=funny-stuff">funny-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311884497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6664680154764240024">I am not sure why, but this book took me completely by surprise. The reviews for this book rated it highly and I knew the narration was reported to be fantastic. But I still got my socks knocked off. This book hooked me from the beginning. What this book is about at its core is a young girl (sophomore in high school) navigating the social mine field of high school and trying to make sense of her female friendships and her relationships with boys. <br/><br/>The setting is perfect – a private school, a scho</span>
  <span id="freeText6664680154764240024" style="display:none">I am not sure why, but this book took me completely by surprise. The reviews for this book rated it highly and I knew the narration was reported to be fantastic. But I still got my socks knocked off. This book hooked me from the beginning. What this book is about at its core is a young girl (sophomore in high school) navigating the social mine field of high school and trying to make sense of her female friendships and her relationships with boys. <br /><br />The setting is perfect – a private school, a scholarship student, a boat house for the main character’s home, some very involved, loving but extremely quirky parents, and lots of mistakes, missteps and misunderstandings. All together, it makes a book that is incredibly funny and enlightening. E. Lockhart really really really hits on what it is like to be a 15 year old girl. Relationships with other girls are so intense at that age, love affairs in a way – but they can be treacherous. And relationships with the opposite sex is a complete mystery, every step brings a new learning moment. This book could just be light and funny and it is definitely that. But it also has serious character growth that brings readers along for the ride. Through Ruby Oliver’s examination of her boyfriend list, she examines what it means to be a true friend, what is the meaning of popularity, how girls get labeled slut, the true actions of betrayal, and that it feels good to have one’s boobs fondled. Yup, all important topics. E. Lockhart has a serious talent of leading Ruby and the reader down the path of enlightenment but doing it in a very fun way (for the reader, for Ruby it is actually quite painful and embarrassing) so that it doesn’t feel like I was learning. Side note, there is even a beautiful feminist discussion on the effect of labeling a female, how men do not get labeled in a similar way, and why this is -- E. Lockhart does this brilliantly by having a teacher discuss this topic in a class presentation, so that it does not come off preachy at all. I have a soft spot for this particular issue and I thought it was really well handled. <br /><br />What was surprising for me was that I ended up identifying with both Ruby Oliver (the lead in this story) and her parents. I hope that I am not quite as boundary ignoring, invasive and quirky as Ruby’s parents were but through them I saw two people who truly loved their daughter and wanted to stay involved in her life. I saw myself talking to my teenager, trying to appear (hopelessly I am sure) cool, try to convey love and yet respect those important boundaries. Raising a teenager is such hard work. This book is a tad bit mature for my 12.5 year old but in a few years I cannot wait for her to read it and then I will ask her, “How did this make you feel?” And she will roll her eyes and walk away. But I will smile, because in a way we will have shared a moment. <br /><br />I recommend this book for anyone who has been a teenager, who has a teenager, and who likes to laugh.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6664680154764240024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1691797130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10756623297337030984">I've had a good run with young adult/ high school based books lately, so my hopes were high for this one. Sadly they were dashed by girlish kissing fantasies and daisy filled daydreams. Okay, it wasn't exactly like that, but near enough compared my teenage years.<br/><br/>This certainly has a charm that will appeal to a lot of people; maybe those who aren't as jaded, sarcastic and generally inappropriate as I am. See, my biggest problem was being unable to relate to any of the characters. Granted it's bee</span>
  <span id="freeText10756623297337030984" style="display:none">I've had a good run with young adult/ high school based books lately, so my hopes were high for this one. Sadly they were dashed by girlish kissing fantasies and daisy filled daydreams. Okay, it wasn't exactly like that, but near enough compared my teenage years.<br /><br />This certainly has a charm that will appeal to a lot of people; maybe those who aren't as jaded, sarcastic and generally inappropriate as I am. See, my biggest problem was being unable to relate to any of the characters. Granted it's been awhile since I was at school, but I still feel 16/17 in my head so whatever. <br /><br />I spent my days at abandoned factories with lots of boys, covered in mud and playing truth or dare. The first penis I saw was a result of that game and in fact wasn't just one penis, it was 6, all flapping about as their owners tried to win a race with their trousers round their ankles. Oh, those were the days.<br /><br />So you see, I wasn't like Ruby. That was my point. I got distracted by the willy Olympics. I should probably mention the book again.<br /><br />Yes, so. The book. I will say this was well written and had some really sweet, humorous moments. A lot of people will be able to relate to Ruby, just not this pervert.</span>

<div id="review_150754013" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Noelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2448124-noelle"><img alt="Noelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492692932p2/2448124.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_302561661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302561661" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302561661?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=rainy-day-re-reads">rainy-day-re-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302561661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16960674998339531374">I can sum up my entire experience reading The Boyfriend List in one word: cathartic. If you don't already have a shrink, you'll probably realize you need to get one after reading this book (or if you're broke like me, the Ruby Oliver books will do just fine). The Boyfriend List isn't your usual contemporary romance. I admit that halfway through the first chapter I declared myself Team Noel (still shipping those two after the book was over but more on that later) but really this book is all Team </span>
  <span id="freeText16960674998339531374" style="display:none">I can sum up my entire experience reading The Boyfriend List in one word: cathartic. If you don't already have a shrink, you'll probably realize you need to get one after reading this book (or if you're broke like me, the Ruby Oliver books will do just fine). The Boyfriend List isn't your usual contemporary romance. I admit that halfway through the first chapter I declared myself Team Noel (still shipping those two after the book was over but more on that later) but really this book is all Team Ruby.<br /><br />Fifteen-year-old Ruby Oliver is having a horrible week. Her boyfriend of six months broke up with her, her best friend started dating her now ex-boyfriend three days later, she has become a "leper" or a loner, and her once perfect reputation has been completely tarnished. Ruby, unable to deal with the current situation of her life, begins expressing her pain and worry in the form of panic attacks. Before she knows it, she's sitting in Dr. Z, her therapist's office, and being told to make a list: The Boyfriend List. Ruby's story is told through her multiple shrink appointments, stories of fifteen guys she's ever liked/kissed/dated, and flashbacks of her life before it became a disaster. <br /><br />From the surface, The Boyfriend List seems like a fluffy and fun read - which it is! But its also so much more. The depth of emotions conveyed and character personalities utterly astounded me. Lockhart writes from a fresh, realistic voice that is easy to relate to. Ruby, despite being the main character, is far from perfect. She continually makes the same mistakes with guys, she fails to see true friendship when it's in front of her eyes, and she yearns for her own Prince Charming called Tommy Hazard. Yet, Ruby is like every other girl in the world. Who hasn't made mistakes with guys? Who hasn't been able to reach their hand out to friendship even when it's right in front of their face? Who doesn't dream about "The One" or their "Mr. Right"? Every girl, no matter what age, will be able to inexplicably relate to Ruby and the debacles she finds herself in.<br /><br />Although Ruby's story is primarily told through the list of boys she writes, it is mainly about friendship, honesty, and truth. Through her appointments with Dr. Z, Ruby is able to uncover the raw truth behind every one of her problems whether they be regarding her best friend Kim, who holds her emotions inside until they burst; her parents, who are stuck in an ever-raging power struggle; or even herself, who is unable to rectify the mistakes she has made and be open with her feelings. More than just a book, The Boyfriend List is like "The Ultimate Girl's Guide to Life." While reading about Ruby, you will find yourself feeling as if you are reading about yourself. Ruby's mistakes are your mistakes. Ruby's friends faults are your friend's faults. Ruby's relationship with her parents is bound to be at least remotely similar to your relationship with your parents. It still shocks me how Ruby's story can correlate so perfectly with that of my, or any other girls, own. <br /><br />The Boyfriend List is a must-read for every girl out there. It is sarcastic, funny, and emotionally-cleansing. It is written in a fun and engaging manner, Ruby's 'voice' is relate-able and refreshing, and most importantly, the ending is realistic and full of promise for more. If there's one thing I've learned from this book, it's that bottling up your emotions is definitely not the solution. So, with my new-found sense of emotional truthfulness I tell you this: Read. This. Book. NOW! There's no way you can't fall in love with it! ;) </span>
  <a data-text-id="16960674998339531374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_183885060" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183885060" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183885060?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7283851-the-boyfriend-list">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=cute">cute</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183885060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16834825966615848338">Therapy - how people used to work through problems before Facebook existed. Nowadays people tend to talk about how much their life sucks on a social network until enough people pop in to console them. Ruby has a therapist, half the world has a Facebook, and I just have Goodreads.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>Reviewing as therapy : Everything you absolutely didn't want to know about my life made available for you to read about in print.</b>
</blockquote><br/>This book made me feel a little bit disturbed about my own high school existence. The e</span>
  <span id="freeText16834825966615848338" style="display:none">Therapy - how people used to work through problems before Facebook existed. Nowadays people tend to talk about how much their life sucks on a social network until enough people pop in to console them. Ruby has a therapist, half the world has a Facebook, and I just have Goodreads.<br><blockquote>
  <b>Reviewing as therapy : Everything you absolutely didn't want to know about my life made available for you to read about in print.</b>
</blockquote><br>This book made me feel a little bit disturbed about my own high school existence. The end notes at the end of the book had the author relaying this - <i>In high school, I used to keep a list of all the boys I ever kissed. There were little hearts dotting the is and everything!</i><br><br>I so can't relate to that. Unless there was a book for how many times you'd cut class to go drinking or hook up with a guy. If that was the case, I could have filled a few books (on cutting, not hook-ups. I didn't actually hook up quite enough times to fill volumes or anything).<br><br>It's all too possible that my now-fading memories of high school are much more badass than reality actually was but for the most part, my life in high school was much more like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119620168" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect Chemistry</a> than it was Ruby Oliver's life. I didn't have cutesy friends who pondered things like boob grabbing and such. That said, I do applaud the author for trying to portray the thought process of girls. Even though I couldn't personally relate to the majority of the book, it was a fun and cute read. The scenes with Ruby's parents were funny because my parents have had some of those "moments."<br><br>This book also makes me wonder what it would have been like if I was parenting girls instead of boys. This is exactly how a conversation would go in my house between my husband and teen son :<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379768960i/273547.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In fact, I can positively say that this exact conversation has happened before. I honestly don't think Ruby Oliver was ever going to have this conversation with her parents!<br><br>I came back to add more to my review after realizing that all I did was talk about myself and not the book. It's as if I was channeling a Ruby-esque therapy session. Something else that also popped into my head tonight is that maybe I honestly can relate more to Ruby than I'd originally thought. If anything, I probably act more like a teenager now than I did when I was actually a teen. At this stage in my life, there's less to be afraid of and if I'm caught dotting some letters with hearts, who cares? I really should get back into letter writing...talk about a lost art form. <br><br>Yes, rambling is my weapon of choice today. What can I say about the book itself? It's quirky. The footnotes are hilarious. Normally, books written in alternate formats such as letter, diary, etc. are a deterrent for me. I thought the use of a therapist format in this book was creative. I have no clue how book 2 is going to go...if it follows the same pattern or not. We shall see.<br><br><b>Ruby is a character :</b><br><br><i>~ I say, thirteen is too many dogs for good mental health. Five is pretty much the limit. More than five dogs and you forfeit your right to call yourself entirely sane.<br><br>~ All the grownups laughed when I said the bunny's name was Cox and I didn't understand why.<br><br></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16834825966615848338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1585685146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7279173097205771499">I read this for the first time in high school, and I remember being just as annoyed by her shitty friends and parents as I was this time around. It was a decent book, but I wanted to punch nearly everyone the entire time. My teenage years didn't look anything like Ruby's, and honestly, I'm glad. Even when I read this for the first time, I remember wanting to shake her and tell her to stop focusing on being one of the "popular kids". <br/><br/>I swear, if this baby I'm carrying right now acts anything like</span>
  <span id="freeText7279173097205771499" style="display:none">I read this for the first time in high school, and I remember being just as annoyed by her shitty friends and parents as I was this time around. It was a decent book, but I wanted to punch nearly everyone the entire time. My teenage years didn't look anything like Ruby's, and honestly, I'm glad. Even when I read this for the first time, I remember wanting to shake her and tell her to stop focusing on being one of the "popular kids". <br /><br />I swear, if this baby I'm carrying right now acts anything like 90% of these characters, I'm going to lose it. Most of them treated everyone like garbage. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7279173097205771499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196341348" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196341348" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4111021-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400812804p2/4111021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196341348?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/4111021-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780385902380" href="/book/show/2041687.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=women-s-lit">women-s-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196341348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14571786839803364426"><br/>Since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301022.The_Boyfriend_List' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>
    <b>The Boyfriend List</b>
  </i>
</a> is a book about lists (<i>15 Guys, 11 Shrink Appointments, 4 Ceramic Frogs, and Me, Ruby Oliver</i>), I think I'm going to go out of the box and write my thoughts on the book in enumeration form, too. My personal sub-title: <b><u>5 Reasons I Liked It, 3 Reasons I Didn't, And A Recommendation</u>.</b><br/><br/><b><u>5 Reasons I Liked It:</u> </b><br/><br/>1. It dealt with high school reality and teen angst/problems, much in the same manner that <a href='http://bookishlittleme.attymonique.com/2011/11/stargirl.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Stargirl</i>
</a> (by Jerry Spinelli) did. Personally, I never experienced </span>
  <span id="freeText14571786839803364426" style="display:none"><br />Since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301022.The_Boyfriend_List" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Boyfriend List</b>
  </i>
</a> is a book about lists (<i>15 Guys, 11 Shrink Appointments, 4 Ceramic Frogs, and Me, Ruby Oliver</i>), I think I'm going to go out of the box and write my thoughts on the book in enumeration form, too. My personal sub-title: <b><u>5 Reasons I Liked It, 3 Reasons I Didn't, And A Recommendation</u>.</b><br /><br /><b><u>5 Reasons I Liked It:</u> </b><br /><br />1. It dealt with high school reality and teen angst/problems, much in the same manner that <a href="http://bookishlittleme.attymonique.com/2011/11/stargirl.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Stargirl</i>
</a> (by Jerry Spinelli) did. Personally, I never experienced anything similar to what the protagonist, Ruby “Roo” Oliver, went through, but I can sympathize. <br /><br />2. The writing was straightforward and simple, and given that it was told in the first person POV, the narrative was exactly like how a 16-year-old would have written it. <br /><br />3. The situation that Roo found herself in elicited not only feelings of sympathy from me, but also disgust and outrage at the people she called her friends. I was affected by it! I was so angry for Roo! <br /><br />4. In between the <i>outrageous </i>and the (sometimes) <i>annoying</i>, there was also the <i>hilarious</i>: Roo's mom, Elaine, a performing artist, having a show where she talked Roo first having her period, for example. It must have been humiliating to have your first period and having your own mother telling the world about it, but it's hilarious at the same time, when you think about it. <br /><br />5. Although the ending could have been so much better, in my opinion, I thought that through her experiences, Roo has learned an important lesson in her young life.  I thought it was wonderful that within the period of an entire school year that she became part of the “in” crowd, had a cool boyfriend, was later on ostracized and called labels (“slut”, “leper”), and had panic attacks which required the shrink appointments, she had truly matured. <br /><br /><b><u>3 Reasons I Didn't</u>: </b><br /><br />1. I hated the footnotes! They tended to distract me from the narrative, especially footnotes that took up half of the page or continued on to the next. <br /><br />2. While it was probably necessary that Roo's story was not told in chronological order, the author having resorted to a see-sawing between the past and the present in order to construct Roo's timeline, it nonetheless annoyed and confused me at times. There was a lot of overlapping of events, in fact, necessitating an explanation of the chronology of events from time to time. (<i>“That was the Friday after the dance, so that would be one week before the so-and-so and three days after the so-and-so.”</i> Something like that.) <br /><br />3. I hated Roo's friends. Loathed them. Especially that Kim. GRRRRR!<br /><br /><b><u>A Recommendation</u>: </b><br /><br />I don't believe that you have to be able to relate to the characters of a book in order to appreciate it, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301022.The_Boyfriend_List" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Boyfriend List</b>
  </i>
</a> is a perfect example. Although I couldn't relate with any one character in it, I liked it because of the social issues that it dealt with: teenage angst, peer pressure, first love and heartbreak, ostracism, labels. Having said that, I would recommend this book to anyone who wants to take a trip down memory lane, back to their own high school years, and remember. :)<br /><br />Original post <a href="http://bookishlittleme.attymonique.com/2012/03/by-e.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14571786839803364426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_198342427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198342427" />
    <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard"><img alt="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321462468p2/2216677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198342427?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307206862" href="/book/show/1220423.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198342427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7560507933221657102"><i>(Note this is a review for the first 3 books. Yes I know that's a lazy cop-out but I've read too many books to properly review lately. Also I'm not really sure why I took away a star and I'm considering giving it back)</i><br/><br/>When I first met Ruby Oliver at the local library, I thought the books looked pretty darned girly. Also it sounded a little bit too boy-crazy. Sometimes I get frustrated with all those true-love YA stories. I want to scream THERES MORE TO LIFE THAN BOYS! Besides, who finds true lov</span>
  <span id="freeText7560507933221657102" style="display:none"><i>(Note this is a review for the first 3 books. Yes I know that's a lazy cop-out but I've read too many books to properly review lately. Also I'm not really sure why I took away a star and I'm considering giving it back)</i><br /><br />When I first met Ruby Oliver at the local library, I thought the books looked pretty darned girly. Also it sounded a little bit too boy-crazy. Sometimes I get frustrated with all those true-love YA stories. I want to scream THERES MORE TO LIFE THAN BOYS! Besides, who finds true love in high school?<br /><br />Oh how judgmental I am sometimes. This series is one of the best that I've read this year. This is not a mushy true love story. It's girly, but the right kind of girly. Ruby is witty, intelligent, neurotic, boy crazy and completely awesome.<br /><br />I'm very impressed how these books touch upon some serious topics without taking themselves too seriously. Sometimes girls treat each other like competition rather than friends. The Ruby Oliver books navigates tough girl friendship situations with humor unlike anything I've seen. But at the same time they acknowledge that sometimes girls suck, especially where boys are concerned. <br /><br />The story starts with Ruby in social exile because she kissed her (former) best friends boyfriend. Never mind that Jackson was Ruby's boyfriend first, or that Jackson kissed Ruby back. None of that matters because the school mob has deemed Ruby a boyfriend stealing slut. (Sidenote: Why is it that the boys are never to blame in these situations?)<br /><br />Ruby's new found social leprosy leads to panic attacks, shrink visits and an unfortunate Xerox of her "Boyfriend list" created for her psychiatrist.<br /><br />It's hard to list every reason I love these books. There's just so much to like. But you know I have to try!<br />1. Ruby's insightful and witty commentary about life<br />2. Neurotic hippie parents who live on a houseboat but clearly love their daughter very much<br />3. Misadventures and confusion with boys<br />4. Noel's fruit roll ups (the second and third book)<br />5. Hooter Protection Agency<br />6. The Boyfriend Book--insightful scientific observations of the male species<br />7. Non-preachy but important commentary on girl friendship and always blaming the girl<br />8. A main character who isn't perfect but is likable<br />9. Silly poems written by boys<br />10. Frogs laden with meaning<br />11. A goat named Robespierre <br />12. Ruby's addiction to making lists<br /><br />Who cares about stars! This book gets a whole box of fruit roll-ups, value sized folks. (I am currently on a fruit roll-up binge so this is a high compliment). It's so much fun, but it's not mindless fun it's SMART fun. I cannot recommend this series enough.<br /><br /><i>If you like audio, these books are excellent. Please note that the narrator changes after book 1. They're still good, but the original narrator is amazing. After a few minutes I didn't really mind the new narrator.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7560507933221657102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_329274531" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329274531" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581282691p2/5501124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329274531?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=review-on-the-blog">review-on-the-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=i-have-a-copy">i-have-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=received-via-book-swap">received-via-book-swap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=female-pov">female-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=favourite-author">favourite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=gave-me-a-toothache">gave-me-a-toothache</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329274531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13127579691101870811"><br/><br/>The Boyfriend List by E.Lockhart is set in Seattle. Ruby Oliver is fifteen years old and lives on a houseboat with her parents, Elaine and Kevin. She attends Tate Prep on a scholarship and up until ten days ago, had a best friend, Kim, and two other close friends, Nora and Cricket. Now she's had a panic attack and is feeling anxious so she starts seeing a psychologist, Dr Z. Dr Z suggests Ruby (or Roo to her friends and family) make a list of all her boyfriends, real or almost, and any other boy</span>
  <span id="freeText13127579691101870811" style="display:none"><br /><br />The Boyfriend List by E.Lockhart is set in Seattle. Ruby Oliver is fifteen years old and lives on a houseboat with her parents, Elaine and Kevin. She attends Tate Prep on a scholarship and up until ten days ago, had a best friend, Kim, and two other close friends, Nora and Cricket. Now she's had a panic attack and is feeling anxious so she starts seeing a psychologist, Dr Z. Dr Z suggests Ruby (or Roo to her friends and family) make a list of all her boyfriends, real or almost, and any other boys she feels she has had a connection or issue with and we're provided with this list at the beginning of the book.<br /><br />I've known about this series for a while, but not knowing if I'd like it, I put off ordering it and I could only find a copy of it at the library that's furthest from me, so I never got around to reading it. Then the wonderful Maggie sent me the first three books and it was love at first sentence. I'm a list-maker so I appreciated Ruby's list and I also enjoyed the funny footnotes that peppered the story, they were all so amusing and added more of Ruby's personality to the story.<br /><br />Speaking of personality, Ruby's is fantastic. I found her voice so realistic and I could listen to her talk all day. Yes, she's a little self involved, but what fifteen year old isn't? She's also caring, loving, intelligent and a teensy bit naive because she didn't see her break up coming or the backstabbing that came along with it. The events that occur, while not life-threatening or world-ending, are important enough to Ruby and they bring on anxiety and panic attacks. I was really happy that she had Dr Z to help her out because I don't think her parents were doing a good job of being there for her.<br /><br />Ruby's mum, Elaine, is a performance artist and an at-home copy editor in between tours. Ruby had to put a stop to her mum using Ruby's life in her performances, eg. a tour based on Ruby getting her first period. Elaine is melodramatic, loud and pushy. She's always harping on about eating disorders and is convinced Ruby has one, even though she doesn't. Instead of listening, she talks over the top of Ruby and her husband, Kevin, who runs a gardening newsletter and seed catalogue.<br /><br />There were so many thoughts that Ruby had that I really latched on to, so many opinions that I shared with her or made me think "that's so true!" I particularly loved the footnote about people calling to say "we need to talk" and then refusing to tell you what it is and then making you wait only to give you bad news, people do this all the time and it can be horrible. The other time I really connected with Roo was when she's with Dr Z, listing all the things she thinks about and she says "I probably think too much" - me too, Roo, me too! Another bonus point, for anyone playing along with me, is that Roo is a vegetarian, win!<br /><br />I really disliked Ruby's ex-boyfriend, Jackson, and she is better off without him, but I understand that it's not always easy to let go. And don't get me started on her so-called friends! Kim, Cricket and Nora turned out to be such stereotypical high school mean girls, ganging up on Ruby without knowing all the facts when they should have been on her side. I was happy with Meghan who it turns out had been there all along and for the spark between Roo and Noel, it gave me butterflies.<br /><br />I want everyone I know to read The Boyfriend List and get to know and love Ruby like I do. I would definitely recommend it to fans of realistic fiction and book set in high school but even if you're not a realistic fic fan, you will probably get a kick out of Ruby.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13127579691101870811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/682102523?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer682102523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12806831233086855631"><i>
  <blockquote>So there I was, my mom yelling at me, Heidi talking crap about me, weirded out by the Noel dynamic, Angelo probably mad at me, Jackson thinking I was cheating on him/getting over him too quickly/generally skanky - and you'd think things couldn't get worse, but ha! It's my life. Things can always get worse.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>It's really too bad I wasn't much of a reader during most of my teens, because there have been times when I seriously could have used some Ruby Oliver in my ridiculously confusing teenage l</span>
  <span id="freeText12806831233086855631" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>So there I was, my mom yelling at me, Heidi talking crap about me, weirded out by the Noel dynamic, Angelo probably mad at me, Jackson thinking I was cheating on him/getting over him too quickly/generally skanky - and you'd think things couldn't get worse, but ha! It's my life. Things can always get worse.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />It's really too bad I wasn't much of a reader during most of my teens, because there have been times when I seriously could have used some Ruby Oliver in my ridiculously confusing teenage life, even if it was just so I'd have someone to relate to. <br /><br />I did actually read <i>The Boyfriend List</i> years ago in Dutch, but I was twelve or thirteen at the time, so boys were still playmates rather than datemates to me. (They still are, to be completely honest, though the connotation of playmate has shifted a little over time. You can judge. I judge Past Ellis all the time.) For some completely unintelligible and probably stupid - see, there we go with the Past Ellis judging - reason, I never continued qith the series. Because this is obviously a mistake I needed to rectify, I decided to make it my personal mission to binge the entire <i>Ruby Oliver</i> series this summer. This is a version of Past Ellis that will never be judged because her decision skills were flawless. I loved <i>The Boyfriend List</i> even more than I did nine or ten years ago. <br /><br />Read the rest on <a href="http://randomtransliterator.blogspot.be/2014/07/review-boyfriend-list.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Random Transliterator</a>.</span>
