<div id="review_1081402913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1081402913" />
    <a title="♥ Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13161862-sarah"><img alt="♥ Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455167556p2/13161862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1081402913?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ Sarah" href="/user/show/13161862-sarah">♥ Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13161862-sarah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1081402913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer266429362660488067"><blockquote><b>My very own soundtrack for this book:</b><br/>Crystal Fighters - You & I <br/>The Lumineers - Charlie Boy <br/>The Lumineers - Flowers in Her Hair<br/>This, the Silent War - We Are Broken<br/>Vance Joy - Riptide<br/>MSMR - Bones <br/>Banks - Waiting Game<br/></blockquote><br/><br/>Sometimes I get this urge to write stuff down. <br/>Mundane day-to-day thoughts, to-do lists, to-read lists, to-buy lists, to-cook lists, to-gift lists, etc. (Clearly, I have a List Writing Addiction, or too much time on my hands.) <br/>I’ve probably created and destroyed and revised a dozen or</span>
  <span id="freeText266429362660488067" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>My very own soundtrack for this book:</b><br />Crystal Fighters - You &amp; I <br />The Lumineers - Charlie Boy <br />The Lumineers - Flowers in Her Hair<br />This, the Silent War - We Are Broken<br />Vance Joy - Riptide<br />MSMR - Bones <br />Banks - Waiting Game<br /></blockquote><br /><br />Sometimes I get this urge to write stuff down. <br />Mundane day-to-day thoughts, to-do lists, to-read lists, to-buy lists, to-cook lists, to-gift lists, etc. (Clearly, I have a List Writing Addiction, or too much time on my hands.) <br />I’ve probably created and destroyed and revised a dozen or more “5-year plans” just this month. <br />I’m always changing my mind, but documenting the process.<br />I am a hopeless planner. <br />It’s just how I am. <br />Even if I have a tendency to change my mind. A lot. <br />I write lists because they give me clarity and purpose; <br />I just like knowing that I can plan things and then execute them. <br /><br /><b>Bottom line: I like being in control. </b><br />It’s most likely a neurotic-control-freak-perfectionist thing. <br />When I write something down, somehow it becomes real for me. <br />Almost like a promise. <br />A reminder on paper that I can touch and see. <br />Evidence. <br />A piece of me (an inconsequential, random thought in my head that I would probably forget forever) now a material part of the world. <br />Documented. <br /><br /><b>But those are the easy things to write. Easy to control. <br /><br />There are other things though, that I can’t quite seem to put into words – or on paper. </b><br /><br />Like, those nostalgic days of your youth; the good memories and the bad. That "growing-up" process. <br /><br />I wouldn’t know where or how to start writing about that stuff. <br /> <br />Sometimes I wonder if those days ever happened at all. Some of the stuff I “endured” seems so petty now. So inconsequential; I wish I could tell my younger self to suck-it-up; to not have been so overly sensitive and over-think things, to not have been so hard myself; to not have cared so much about what others thought of me; that it was okay that I made those mistakes - that no one is perfect; to forgive and not to have been so harsh; to not have gotten drunk that one night at that one party junior year, to never have fallen in love with that one boy, etc. <br /><br />Other times, I wonder how I ever got through those maddening days – those early years of heartbreak and pain and betrayals and losses. <br /><br />And then there are those happy memories of the firsts and the butterflies and the laughing and the carelessness and discovering a whole new world, of possibilities, and the what-if’s. Sometimes, I can’t even believe that was ME back then. That those things happened to me – and those memories belong to ME, not some character in a book, or in a movie, or from my fantasies. <br /><br /><b>This book does just that. It articulates all of the things you wish you could (but never could), into words, unto paper.</b><br /><br />It takes you back to the days of your own firsts, then to the days of heartbreak, confusion, betrayal, teenage girl-drama, and of course – the bane and crux of existence in those days – boys. It takes you to that dark period in your life where you saw and felt and breathed only your misery. It forcibly keeps you in there, yet at the same time, makes you confront it and work through it. <br /><br /><b>Ruby ("Roo") was definitely not the perfect heroine, but I loved her so much more for her mistakes - her flaws - her insecurities;</b> for her glaring honesty, her timely humor, her sarcasm, her unapologetic view on life and love and friendship; her unyielding loyalty, her overly sentimental, sensitive, over-thinking, over-explaining, push-over, boy-crazy list-making, panic-attack prone self. I loved her for it all. And I saw glimpses of myself, my story in hers. And I laughed. So much. But at the same time, felt like crying, too. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart" title="E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">E. Lockhart</a> just has that magical writing quality. <br /><br />I read and loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars" title="We Were Liars by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">We Were Liars</a> first. I know I’m 8 or so years late for this book, but never once did this book feel dated. Just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars" title="We Were Liars by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">We Were Liars</a>, the universal themes in this book – especially on loss and heartbreak was so beautifully captured in this brilliantly funny (foot-note included) coming-of-age story. Another exquisitely written YA gem; highly recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="266429362660488067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightreads" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads">Lightreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154418053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4344925338025424599">Described to me as one of the best high school girl romantic shenanigans confessionals out there. I think this might actually be true – high school was just ten years ago for me in real time, even if it was much longer in soultime, and this book feels very familiar and authentic to me. It just had no aliens. Or ghosts, or demons, or telepaths – basically, no one had to save the world, so it didn’t kick up to awesome for me.<br/><br/>That, and the much more important thing. The shtick here is that our narr</span>
  <span id="freeText4344925338025424599" style="display:none">Described to me as one of the best high school girl romantic shenanigans confessionals out there. I think this might actually be true – high school was just ten years ago for me in real time, even if it was much longer in soultime, and this book feels very familiar and authentic to me. It just had no aliens. Or ghosts, or demons, or telepaths – basically, no one had to save the world, so it didn’t kick up to awesome for me.<br /><br />That, and the much more important thing. The shtick here is that our narrator is talking to her therapist as part of her treatment for a mild anxiety disorder resulting from some difficult adolescent shenanigans. And the sessions are structured around the boys in her life, one chapter for each.<br /><br />Yeah. This book is like the anti-Bechtel test. It’s about self-empowerment and speaking up and crediting your own desires, and the whole fucking thing is two women sitting there talking about nothing but men. The structure takes the empowering message, drags it out back and double-taps it to the forehead, then scribbles “boys boys boys!” all over its face in sparkly pen, is what I’m saying.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4344925338025424599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer617324500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7355442075299276790">I first came across E.Lockhart with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars' title='We Were Liars by E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>We Were Liars</a> which, to be honest, I preferred on the second read. I then read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11113790.The_Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks' title='The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks by E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a> which was fab and I decided that this is probably a writer for me. I like how she explores relationships and the inner workings of a teenage mind.<br/>Although this book was just as clever, I really didn't like Ruby. She is one of those popular (but not 'most' popular) girls at school who is completely oblivious to others, and their feelin</span>
  <span id="freeText7355442075299276790" style="display:none">I first came across E.Lockhart with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars" title="We Were Liars by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">We Were Liars</a> which, to be honest, I preferred on the second read. I then read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11113790.The_Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks" title="The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a> which was fab and I decided that this is probably a writer for me. I like how she explores relationships and the inner workings of a teenage mind.<br />Although this book was just as clever, I really didn't like Ruby. She is one of those popular (but not 'most' popular) girls at school who is completely oblivious to others, and their feelings. So being in her head for the whole book was tough when she wasn't someone I would want to be friends with.<br />But it was an easy enough read, and she does actually make some progress by the end.<br />There are a few more books in the series, but I think I am done. I'll read something else by Lockhart instead</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694730719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16105176681048497328">The Ruby Oliver books are like the American equivalent of the Georgia Nicholson books in the UK. The girls are just as obsessed with boys and relationships and drama, with the same type of humour and style. It's not really my thing, because the characters feel so immature and I was never that kind of 15 year old, so I don't think I'll finish the series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_154260093" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154260093" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154260093?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471405969" href="/book/show/30323739-the-boyfriend-list">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jasprit by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2016">out-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154260093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5349278854623159811">This book was such a refreshing read, I'd gone into it thinking that it'd be a sort of young read for me, but I'm glad that this wasn't the case for me at all. It did take me some time getting used to Ruby and what was going on in her life, but once I got into The Boyfriend List I absolutely adored Ruby. She was such refreshing character, her voice and everything that she was going through just spoke volumes for me. What she had to go through was truly awful, the turn of events and how people tu</span>
  <span id="freeText5349278854623159811" style="display:none">This book was such a refreshing read, I'd gone into it thinking that it'd be a sort of young read for me, but I'm glad that this wasn't the case for me at all. It did take me some time getting used to Ruby and what was going on in her life, but once I got into The Boyfriend List I absolutely adored Ruby. She was such refreshing character, her voice and everything that she was going through just spoke volumes for me. What she had to go through was truly awful, the turn of events and how people turned on her, (I also had an inkling about this one particular character and just wished Ruby had been able to realise what a douche they were earlier on) just made me super mad. But despite the lacklustre events and panic attacks that Ruby still attempted to hold her head up high, it couldn't have been easy for anyone for things to change so dramatically in a week. I liked how through seeing a therapist Ruby was able to take a step back and truly see what was going on with her life, the self-reflections and realisations could be daunting at first, but I appreciated the person Ruby became by the end of this book. Lockhart bought so much depth to this book with Ruby's story and gave us such a realistic portrayal of what a teenage life can be like. What I also enjoyed about this book was that despite things hitting the fan with Ruby, Lockhart still managed to bring so much laughter and fun to the story, Ruby was also such a funny character, that you couldn't but laugh at some of the situations she found herself in. The addition of footnotes I did find confusing at first, but this may have been because I was reading the e-book version, and I had to keep flipping back and forth to find the right footnote reference, but after this initial confusion, I couldn't get enough of them! The Boyfriend List was a great start to a new series for me, I can't wait to continue with Ruby's Journey in the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5349278854623159811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_505330558" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/505330558" />
    <a title="Sophie (Blame Chocolate) *on hiatus*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16392175-sophie-blame-chocolate-on-hiatus"><img alt="Sophie (Blame Chocolate) *on hiatus*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590859492p2/16392175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/505330558?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie (Blame Chocolate) *on hiatus*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie (Blame Chocolate) *on hiatus*" href="/user/show/16392175-sophie-blame-chocolate-on-hiatus">Sophie (Blame Chocolate) *on hiatus*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392175-sophie-blame-chocolate-on-hiatus?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392175-sophie-blame-chocolate-on-hiatus?shelf=teenage-life">teenage-life</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer505330558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8524720787998200386">This was actually a lot more enjoyable than I thought it would be! <br/><br/>For starters, it was a really quick and easy read. The only reason it took me longer to finish it was because I had a busy weekend and didn't really have the time to sit down and pick it up most of the time - otherwise, I'd be done with it in under three hours, tops.<br/><br/>Secondly, it was such a light and funny story. It wasn't laugh out loud funny, though, more like a "smiling throughout" and "the occasional chuckle" kind of funny, wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8524720787998200386" style="display:none">This was actually a lot more enjoyable than I thought it would be! <br /><br />For starters, it was a really quick and easy read. The only reason it took me longer to finish it was because I had a busy weekend and didn't really have the time to sit down and pick it up most of the time - otherwise, I'd be done with it in under three hours, tops.<br /><br />Secondly, it was such a light and funny story. It wasn't laugh out loud funny, though, more like a "smiling throughout" and "the occasional chuckle" kind of funny, which is perfectly fine in my book.<br /><br />Ruby (or "Roo") probably reminds a lot of readers of their own teenage selves and I am no exception. While some of the things that happened in the book sometimes frustrated me and made me want to roll my eyes, they were exceedingly real. I remember acting like Ruby and thinking like Ruby when I was that age, and reading about it made me realise just how naive and idiotic we can all be at that age! (Again, perfectly fine and real.)<br /><br />I also suffered a bit with anxiety and panic attacks when I was younger (still do, but on a much lesser scale), so I could definitely relate to the symptons and the way it was described. I still felt it was a subject that wasn't explored enough, however, and instead took a back seat while the romance and teenage angst/drama remained center stage. It was one of the things I would have liked the author to have explored more and really made it seem like a big issue to Roo - most of the time, it felt like an afterthought of a plot device. I felt it was brushed off a bit too much and not given the attention/importance it deserved, which was a bit disappointing. <br /><br />Instead, we get all these teenage issues that make it seem like the world is about to end at any moment and/or everyone is out there to get you: the complicated relationships, the path to finding yourself and understanding your place in the world, the confusion surrounding you almost 24/7 and the thought that you are never good enough/are not going something right yet have no idea what that something is. Things that you will only learn later on actually matter very little in the grand scheme of things.<br /><br />I thought that was well portrayed and we get all these interesting characters with a story to tell. The book definitely touches on worthy topics, yet had some trouble exploring them properly. I get that this is YA and it's supposed to be a very light novel with a carefree undertone to it, and delving into any of those topics at a deeper level would probably create the exact opposite effect: a gloomy, depressing and very triggering contemporary. And I was perfectly okay with it not going that way, either. But a bit more development would have been nice.<br /><br />One other thing I had mixed feelings about were the footnotes. They were a peculiar enough addition but most of the time they explained what I (and probably half the planet) already knew and/or just felt redundant. Funny at times, though.<br /><br />This certainly gave me an Easy A/The Scarlet Letter sort of vibe, which was interesting even if it was not the central focus of the story. I also liked the ending - I was expecting something completely different and predictable but the author thankfully didn't go there! I know there are still more books in this series so there's a lot of space for improvement and/or development (and also space for the author to screw up a perfectly cool message!) but I'm not sure I'll be reading those any time soon.<br /><br />My teenage self would have enjoyed these books immensely but at this stage in my life they are really just meant to amuse me and take me out of a reading slump. Which it absolutely did, so no complaints there! Even though I devoured it in a few hours, it really is nothing amazing or earth-shattering... But it's not meant to me and that's okay.<br /><br />* This was book #2 in the O.W.L.s Readathon * Arithmacy Completed! *<br /><br />3.5/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="8524720787998200386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_474075499" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474075499" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474075499?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7283851-the-boyfriend-list">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=on-my-shelves">on-my-shelves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=owned-print-copy">owned-print-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474075499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1443868308718145264">When I started reading this, I added it on Goodreads and sort of scrolled through reviews, not reading them but eyeing the ratings. For most books, my friends reach a sort of general consensus; with The Boyfriend List, the ratings varied from one star to five. Thankfully, I fell on the higher end of the spectrum, a relief since I just bought the complete series in a fit of no will power.<br/><br/>The variety in opinions on this book makes perfect sense, though. How you feel about The Boyfriend List will l</span>
  <span id="freeText1443868308718145264" style="display:none">When I started reading this, I added it on Goodreads and sort of scrolled through reviews, not reading them but eyeing the ratings. For most books, my friends reach a sort of general consensus; with The Boyfriend List, the ratings varied from one star to five. Thankfully, I fell on the higher end of the spectrum, a relief since I just bought the complete series in a fit of no will power.<br /><br />The variety in opinions on this book makes perfect sense, though. How you feel about The Boyfriend List will likely have a direct correlation to how you feel about the MC, Ruby Oliver. Ruby has a very distinct way of expressing herself and somewhat controversial opinions. If she annoys you, the book will be utter hell. However, if you think she's hilarious and makes good points and maybe reminds you of your high school self, you'll think she and this book are the best ever.<br /><br />Though I did not personally identify with Ruby, I did think that she was funny most of the time, with occasional forays into whininess or melodrama, though these fit her personality and her situation perfectly. The Boyfriend List revolves around a series of panic attacks Ruby had, leading her parents to send her to a therapist. Her therapist asked her to draw up a list of boys for them to discuss. Thus the list was born, ultimately with some Harriet the Spy kind of consequences.<br /><br />What Lockhart got just right is the teenage drama. Ruby feels so much like a teenage girl, with her own misconceptions, weird slang and inability to deal with being a social outcast. Having a boyfriend matters so much. Her own world matters so much, and she has a lot of trouble seeing past her own issues. Her parents fight all the time, but she can't really see that until therapy, and the same goes for her friends' issues too. Ruby has blinders on, and it's wonderful to watch her gain new perspective on the world in her conversations with her shrink.<br /><br />The romantic drama herein depicted may seem a bit like the absurdity of Gossip Girl or Glee, where the same twelve characters keep swapping boyfriends in an endless spiral of jealousy, betrayal and infidelity. However, Tate, Ruby's school, is this tiny prep school full of rich kids (except for Ruby, who's on scholarship); there just aren't that many fish in the dating pool. I went to a very small college, and one guy dated three girls out of the twelve on my freshman hall, so that kind of stuff does happen, though there was no drama with our instance. They're stuck in a small school with lots of hormones and not many people with whom to exercise them.<br /><br />The other awesome thing about Ruby Oliver is that it's not romanticizing teens or trying to depict them as innocent or sex as awful. Ruby discusses sex openly and with overt fascination. She and her friends discuss boys and all of their exploits and that's just so much how life goes down; we all share the details with our best friends.<br /><br />Now, this really does not affect my opinion of the novel or mean anything to those who have not read this book, but I still need to get this off my chest: Kim and Jackson are major d-bags. Jackson especially. He's a serial boyfriend, dumping one girl and immediately lining up the next (or already having her waiting). Kim may be a big proponent of "The Rules," and, yes, Ruby broke them too, but Kim stepped out of line first. She can talk about fate or how it only just happened all she wanted, but she is lying. Ruby needs to get those two awful people out of her heart entirely and out of her life as much as is possible at Tate.<br /><br />The Boyfriend List is a humorous, sassy contemporary, sure to delight those who delight in misadventure, pop culture references, and romantic drama.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1443868308718145264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_210299864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210299864" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/210299864?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7283851-the-boyfriend-list">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tbr-challenge">tbr-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=chick-lit-challenge-2012">chick-lit-challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=ya-realistic-fiction-challenge-2012">ya-realistic-fiction-challenge-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer210299864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14214714867951502579"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I really liked this, and found many moments where I just wanted to give Ruby Oliver a big hug. She goes through a lot of ups and downs in her relationships in the course of the work, and I definitely felt the bumps in the road along with her. That's not to say that I thought this work was perfect. There were aspects of it that I couldn't completely throw myself into, and I think I may need a little while to think about how to best explain those. Still, I'm all for continuing th</span>
  <span id="freeText14214714867951502579" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I really liked this, and found many moments where I just wanted to give Ruby Oliver a big hug. She goes through a lot of ups and downs in her relationships in the course of the work, and I definitely felt the bumps in the road along with her. That's not to say that I thought this work was perfect. There were aspects of it that I couldn't completely throw myself into, and I think I may need a little while to think about how to best explain those. Still, I'm all for continuing this series. I'm too invested in Ruby's story to stop.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />"The Boyfriend List" is a young adult chick-lit novel with a lot of heart, showing the journey of one young woman who endures a rough week of navigating her relationships, family life, and ultimately trying to find ways to be honest with herself as well as the people around her. I did not expect to enjoy this novel as much as I did, but it was well worth the journey. It's a tough read in spurts, and I'll admit it takes the reader out of the comfort zone of one of your typical cutesy reads and showcases some of the flaws that the heroine has while running her through some rough patches.<br /><br />Ruby Oliver is a sweetheart, and its easy to get to know her through the course of the novel. Though when we meet her in the beginning of the novel, she's had one of the worst weeks of her life and suffers from panic attacks, thus needing to see a shrink to deal with her respective problems. One of the requirements in her therapy sessions is to craft a "boyfriend" list. So she crafts a list of every boy she's had a relationship with (even those whom she's never exactly talked to, but still had an impression of some sort with). We learn a lot about Ruby's respective relationships, and in the moments they go wrong, they go VERY wrong.<br /><br />But Ruby is a resilient young lady. While things in her life seem to hit the wall many a time, and she's both betrayed and inadvertently hurts quite a few people along the way, she finds a way to push through, both in her therapy sessions and in her life. This book presents many lessons on the art of acceptance and letting go. That's a lesson that even adults have a hard time swallowing, so with some of the things Ruby faces in this book - I wanna hug her, not just in light of the tough times, but how she ultimately learns to rise above it.<br /><br />I did have a few qualms about "The Boyfriend List" in retrospect, though. I kinda wish the ending of this book had a little more closure. I kept thinking there would be a little more resolution, but alas that point didn't really tie off as well as I was hoping. I'll admit I was also frustrated at how transparent the other characters were at times), but ultimately, I think for what the novel was showing in its real approach to issues in dating, relationships, friendships, and self-acceptance, it worked.<br /><br />I think teens will certainly enjoy this eye-opening read, and I definitely enjoyed what it brought to the table. I found it cute, funny, eye-opening, and with a strong backbone to the themes it tackles. Certainly recommended, and I can't wait to read more in E. Lockhart's respective series.<br /><br />Overall score: 4/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="14214714867951502579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer500026570" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13951318171505595955">OK, I tried, I really did. I listened to the whole thing from the beginning to the end and I just didn't like it. I can see how others would like it, but for me I didn't. I just don't care for stories with boy crazy girls. It's just not the kind of books that I tend to like. You may ask, “if you don't like such stories, then why read this one in the first place?” Easy, I suspected I didn't and finishing this confirmed my suspicions. Also, because I can! “Hmm, OK then, so because of the subject y</span>
  <span id="freeText13951318171505595955" style="display:none">OK, I tried, I really did. I listened to the whole thing from the beginning to the end and I just didn't like it. I can see how others would like it, but for me I didn't. I just don't care for stories with boy crazy girls. It's just not the kind of books that I tend to like. You may ask, “if you don't like such stories, then why read this one in the first place?” Easy, I suspected I didn't and finishing this confirmed my suspicions. Also, because I can! “Hmm, OK then, so because of the subject you didn't like it?” Well yes and no. I didn't like it because I'd rather not read about teens and their semi sex lives. It's not for me. I don't want to read about how being 13 is sooo incredibly old for your first kiss. That's just me though. Totally not judging anyone who enjoyed the book for what it was. <br /><br />I started out with the print book but ended up setting it aside. I couldn't get into the story and the sheer amount of footnotes was just insane. But one of the ladies here on GR (Heidi!) really enjoyed the book and wanted me to try it out. I decided to pick up the audio because I'm kind of addicted to audiobooks. I enjoyed the narrator, Mandy Seigfried. This was my first time hearing her as a narrator and I thought she did a great job. She made Roo sound so realistic. She definitely made the book easier for me to digest. <br /><br />I thought Ruby had pretty crappy and dense friends. Not very supportive and too quick to let a guy come between them. Plus, if ever a friend kisses someones boyfriend, there's equal blame. Her parents should have taken a step back and gave their daughter a talk about self esteem and why it's important. At least help her find a guy that will respect her and treat her like a dude should.<br /><br />In the end, I did not hate it, but I did not like it. Though I didn't think it was as funny as almost all the other readers, I can see how Roo would be very enjoyable for most. I have no one that I would recommend it to. I have not given up on the author, and actually have another one of her books here waiting for me to read.</span>

<div id="review_4289912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carly" href="/user/show/48360-carly">Carly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Cassette 9781400098880" href="/book/show/1134041.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">me?</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48360-carly?shelf=alreadyread-childrensbooks">alreadyread-childrensbooks</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4289912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11442103242960262870">Before I write a detailed review, I think I should make it clear that I fell HARD for this book right from the first page. I am blindly and irregretably in love with it, and I think it's probably an irrational love, so everything I say about it should be taken with a grain of salt.<br/><br/>I have never fallen in love with a book before like I fell in love with this one, right from the beginning and never letting up, only growing more and more intense as time and pages went on. The book is like someone yo</span>
  <span id="freeText11442103242960262870" style="display:none">Before I write a detailed review, I think I should make it clear that I fell HARD for this book right from the first page. I am blindly and irregretably in love with it, and I think it's probably an irrational love, so everything I say about it should be taken with a grain of salt.<br /><br />I have never fallen in love with a book before like I fell in love with this one, right from the beginning and never letting up, only growing more and more intense as time and pages went on. The book is like someone you just think is so wonderful that you can't bear to see their faults, no matter how horrible they are, no matter how glaring, no matter what. Anything misshapen or incorrect or thoughtless simply appears as charmingly artistic.<br /><br />I would give this book six stars if I could. I want to go out and buy it right now. In hardcover. It would be worth every penny. I would drive for hours to buy this book. There is something so, so beautiful about it and I can't even explain it. It resonates with me. It IS me, in a way.<br /><br />The author really has a way with names. Every name in this book is delicate and a work of art. I hold everyone else up to Tim O'Brien's standard of naming characters, because I think he is and always will be the absolute master of picking beautiful, perfect names for his characters. E. Lockhart comes alarmingly close to Tim O'Brien's naming finesse with the characters in this book. Ruby Oliver. Cricket McCall. Kim Yamamoto. Jackson Clarke. Noel DuBoise. Shiv Neel. Finn Murphy. Tommy Hazard.<br /><br />I physically feel my heart expanding when I think about this book. I don't know. For me, I really think it is otherworldly.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sylwia (Wish Fulfillment)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylwia (Wish Fulfillment)" href="/user/show/7476945-sylwia-wish-fulfillment">Sylwia (Wish Fulfillment)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351528556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6900207521439220966"><b>Why I Recommend Moving This UP On Your TBR:</b><br/>· The narrative examined a lot of harmful topics in an enlightened way, for example girl-hate is explored, as is the word "slut", etc.<br/>· This contains an abundance of thought-provoking topics.<br/>· It provides education for readers about certain harmful social behaviors they might be engaging in that hurt others and themselves that they might not even realize.<br/>· The story is well-crafted in that it's unpredictable and all of the chapters weave together well. </span>
  <span id="freeText6900207521439220966" style="display:none"><b>Why I Recommend Moving This UP On Your TBR:</b><br />· The narrative examined a lot of harmful topics in an enlightened way, for example girl-hate is explored, as is the word "slut", etc.<br />· This contains an abundance of thought-provoking topics.<br />· It provides education for readers about certain harmful social behaviors they might be engaging in that hurt others and themselves that they might not even realize.<br />· The story is well-crafted in that it's unpredictable and all of the chapters weave together well. I especially appreciated the way the author used the parents.<br />· I loved the way the author structured the story around "the list".<br />· The portrayal of a therapist and therapy was great! <br /><br /><b>Depending On Your Personal Preferences:</b><br />· All of the characters are extremely flawed in believable ways that are appropriate for their age/development.<br />· This contains a psychoanalytic take on anxiety, rather than the common cognitive-behavioral take that's used now.<br />· This is a break-up story, not a love story.<br />· There is a lot of distance between the reader and all of the other characters. We are stuck deeply in Ruby's head.<br /><br /><b>Why You Might Move This Down On Your TBR:</b><br />· Ruby says some unenlightened stuff about folks who go to therapy. This seems to have been meant as a way to make Ruby a relatable teenager to younger audiences reading it, but it can be harmful.</span>

<div id="review_74872379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74872379" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74872379?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74872379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16503728833361961790">E. Lockhart definitely delivered a heartfelt book with laugh out loud moments that captured my attention and sympathy from cover to cover. <br/><br/><b>The Boyfriend List</b> has what it takes to have you falling for the main character Ruby “Roo” Oliver as her life at Tate Prep turns upside down when her boyfriend dumps her, she begins to suffer from anxiety attacks and ultimately becomes a patient of Dr. Z to deal with her angst. Well you think when she begins to seek counsel, her life will begin to get back on</span>
  <span id="freeText16503728833361961790" style="display:none">E. Lockhart definitely delivered a heartfelt book with laugh out loud moments that captured my attention and sympathy from cover to cover. <br /><br /><b>The Boyfriend List</b> has what it takes to have you falling for the main character Ruby “Roo” Oliver as her life at Tate Prep turns upside down when her boyfriend dumps her, she begins to suffer from anxiety attacks and ultimately becomes a patient of Dr. Z to deal with her angst. Well you think when she begins to seek counsel, her life will begin to get back on track. Not so much. As part of her therapy, she writes a list of fifteen boys that ever meant something to her and makes the grand mistake of throwing her draft copy away in the trash… at school. You’ll have to read the book to figure out why that was such a huge mistake. AG!!!!<br /><br />I loved the book. It was fun, quick to read, engaging and worth every minute I spent angsting over Roo's life. I definitely recommend this to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1629601.The_Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks" title="The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a>, as you'll quickly identify the voice Lockhart pens so well of a strong, flawed and vulnerable teenage girl. I loved it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16503728833361961790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20704468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20704468" />
    <a title="Joanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/300471-joanna"><img alt="Joanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203663686p2/300471.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20704468?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna" href="/user/show/300471-joanna">Joanna</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385732062" href="/book/show/1259132.The_Boyfriend_List">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/300471-joanna?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/300471-joanna?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/300471-joanna?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20704468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11196569546764772094">I was afraid I wouldn't love this book as much the 2nd time--but it's possible I loved it more. I think this book makes my all-time top 20. If I weren't so sleepy, I could wax eloquently about all the qualities that make The Boyfriend List close to perfect; instead, I give you this excerpt, when Ruby Oliver goes on a movie date with a boy she barely knows:<br/><br/>"About a quarter into it, Cabbie put his arm around me and, seconds later, he dangled his right hand down over my shoulder and squeezed my boo</span>
  <span id="freeText11196569546764772094" style="display:none">I was afraid I wouldn't love this book as much the 2nd time--but it's possible I loved it more. I think this book makes my all-time top 20. If I weren't so sleepy, I could wax eloquently about all the qualities that make The Boyfriend List close to perfect; instead, I give you this excerpt, when Ruby Oliver goes on a movie date with a boy she barely knows:<br /><br />"About a quarter into it, Cabbie put his arm around me and, seconds later, he dangled his right hand down over my shoulder and squeezed my boob! We'd hardly even had a conversation before that night--but he went straight for the boob squeeze as if it was the most normal thing in the world.[...] He ended up feeling my boob for the whole movie! He ate popcorn with his left hand and got lucky with his right. It started to feel kind of lopsided, for the right one to get literally an hour and a half's worth of attention and the left one to be all on its lonesome. I barely knew what the movie was about, because I was thinking about my boob the whole time. My boob, being stroked by a near-complete stranger, a big meaty rugby player."<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11196569546764772094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4tVHMXWL26+EEkIUdAAQb+30PlX3qQPd4Len7UhAeo9ij6WTZQv5i4gzXVibp5s2YZbhOD0taA9XVMNoK9Dx2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FCT/i/75uCTC4IF9HvLZxzoxLqLPciwmgKBOXjbZApGUfh0p7nmaAM7BnjHxVVKetlPxzwX2R/Q3QyrbVUmJxA==')})
  }

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I'm not telling you what I look like in any detail. I hate those endless descriptions of a heroine's physical attributes... First of all, it's boring. You should be able to imagine me without all the gory details of my hairstyle or the size of my thighs. And second, it really bothers me how in books it seems like the only two choices are perfection or self-hatred. As if readers will only like a character who's ideal - or completely shattered. Give me a break. People have <i>got</i> to be smarter than that.&rdquo;</span>
